        </div><div class="casAbstract">Access to clean, affordable and reliable energy has been a cornerstone of the world's increasing prosperity and economic growth since the beginning of the industrial revolution.  Our use of energy in the twenty-first century must also be sustainable.  Solar and water-based energy generation, and engineering of microbes to produce biofuels are a few examples of the alternatives.  This Perspective puts these opportunities into a larger context by relating them to a no. of aspects in the transportation and electricity generation sectors.  It also provides a snapshot of the current energy landscape and discusses several research and development opportunities and pathways that could lead to a prosperous, sustainable and secure energy future for the world.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr0LqWT7jFLTrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlgtRy783JqQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xht1WktL7J&amp;md5=4578b112cc957edb201691be3bf606c5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1021/cr500177a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tian, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanowire Electrodes for Electrochemical Energy Storage Devices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanowire Electrodes for Electrochemical Energy Storage Devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mai, Liqiang; Tian, Xiaocong; Xu, Xu; Chang, Liang; Xu, Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">114</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11828-11862</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review on nanowire electrodes for electrochem. energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLJto8eyeBJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lij-gEnozsQ0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs12kurvI&amp;md5=d05bdbd46e32e8f16ce366e6fec607c7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2009.11.048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scrosati, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garche, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium Batteries: Status, Prospects and Future</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium batteries are characterized by high specific energy, high efficiency and long life.  These unique properties have made lithium batteries the power sources of choice for the consumer electronics market with a prodn. of the order of billions of units per yr.  These batteries are also expected to find a prominent role as ideal electrochem. storage systems in renewable energy plants, as well as power systems for sustainable vehicles, such as hybrid and elec. vehicles.  However, scaling up the lithium battery technol. for these applications is still problematic since issues such as safety, costs, wide operational temp. and materials availability, are still to be resolved.  This review focuses first on the present status of lithium battery technol., then on its near future development and finally it examines important new directions aimed at achieving quantum jumps in energy and power content.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpF3KOlj2NuArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lij-gEnozsQ0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXivF2htQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=7273fa7f9f8dd9462c29aac1df0c7420</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/anie.200702505"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bruce, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8fb_of3unOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5884-5901</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8fb_of3unOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01782a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ong, S. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hautier, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jain, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Moore, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceder, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Voltage, Stability and Diffusion Barrier Differences between Sodium-Ion and Lithium-Ion Intercalation Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">9</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3680</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3688</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3680-3688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosFyTQ7K1B3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8fb_of3unOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1CqsLzK&amp;md5=5a6e72a3ae5ebf92d84322240b2c29cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1149/1.1379565"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahn, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Mechanisms of Lithium and Sodium Insertion in Carbon Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The mechanisms of lithium and sodium insertion in carbon materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stevens, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors compare the interactions of lithium and sodium with a range of carbon materials in electrochem. cells.  Through wide angle in situ x-ray scattering studies, both lithium and sodium can be inserted into the interlayer space in disordered carbon materials.  This insertion process is accompanied by an increase in the interlayer spacing in these materials.  Small-angle in situ scattering studies are presented to clearly show the insertion of lithium and sodium into nanopores within disordered hard carbons.  Also very little, if any, sodium can be inserted into graphitic materials in contrast to the large capacity seen for lithium insertion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOuo4QAURxurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8fb_of3unOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXlvFKntr0%253D&amp;md5=15fc03ac3de24271573ed94315375242</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Matsuda, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ishii, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cumings, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4033</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfxJE-KkhuuQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.05.116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Stable and Ultrafast Electrode Reaction of Graphite for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly stable and ultrafast electrode reaction of graphite for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Hu, Zhe; Niu, Zhiqiang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion battery is a potential sustainable energy storage system due to its abundance and low cost.  To date, some Na-storage anode materials have achieved long life span, but the rate performance still remains insufficient.  Herein, in some linear ether-based electrolytes, graphite can not only render unprecedented cyclability (∼6000 cycles), but also exhibit ultrahigh rate capability (up to 10 A g-1), along with a reversible capacity of ∼110 mAh g-1.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Metal Scaffold Supported Bicontinuous Silicon Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Huigang; Braun, Paul V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2778-2783</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si-based Li-ion battery anodes are attracting significant attention because of Si's exceptionally high Li capacity.  However, Si's large vol. change during cycling generally leads to anode pulverization unless the Si is dispersed throughout a matrix in nanoparticulate form.  Because pulverization results in a loss of elec. connectivity, the reversible capacity of most Si anodes decays within a few cycles.  Here the authors report a 3-dimensional (3D) bicontinuous Si anode formed by depositing a layer of Si on the surface of a colloidal crystal templated porous Ni metal scaffold, which maintains elec. connectivity during cycling due to the scaffold.  The porous metal framework serves to both impart elec. cond. to the anode and accommodate the large vol. change of Si upon lithiation and de-lithiation.  The initial capacity of the bicontinuous Si anode is 3568 (Si basis) and 1450 mA-h/g (including the metal framework) at 0.05 C.  After 100 cycles at 0.3 C, 85% of the capacity remains.  Compared to a foil-supported Si film, the 3-dimensional bicontinuous Si anode exhibits significantly improved mech. stability and cycleability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCybPv2P_oHbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfxJE-KkhuuQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XmvFGhurk%253D&amp;md5=e17a640a1f9bf143a498cd8e075b069a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darwiche, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Marino, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sougrati, M. T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fraisse, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stievano, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Monconduit, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfxJE-KkhuuQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta11568b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Baggetto, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ganesh, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, C.-N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meisner, R. M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intrinsic Thermodynamic and Kinetic Properties of Sb Electrodes for Li-Ion and Na-Ion Batteries: Experiment and Theory</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">1</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">27</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7985</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7994</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ta11568b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D7985-7994%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26issue%3D27%26author%3DL.%2BBaggetto%26author%3DP.%2BGanesh%26author%3DC.-N.%2BSun%26author%3DR.%2BA.%2BMeisner%26author%3DT.%2BA.%2BZawodzinski%26author%3DG.%2BM.%2BVeith%26title%3DIntrinsic%2BThermodynamic%2Band%2BKinetic%2BProperties%2Bof%2BSb%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BLi-Ion%2Band%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%253A%2BExperiment%2Band%2BTheory%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ta11568b&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11544&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ta11568b&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intrinsic thermodynamic and kinetic properties of Sb electrodes for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries: experiment and theory</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Baggetto, Loic; Ganesh, P.; Sun, Che-Nan; Meisner, Roberta A.; Zawodzinski, Thomas A.; Veith, Gabriel M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7985-7994</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A detailed comparative study between the electrochem. lithiation and sodiation of pure Sb, relating changes in structural, thermodn., kinetic and electrochem. properties was carried out.  For this purpose, a wide range of measurements using electrochem. (galvanostatic cycling, GITT, PITT), XRD and XPS methods as well as d. functional theory (DFT) based studies have been undertaken.  Assessment of the thermodn. reveals that the reaction proceeds identically during the 1st and 2nd cycles for Li whereas it differs between the 1st and subsequent cycles for Na as the reaction with Na proceeds through a different pathway assocd. with the formation of amorphous NaxSb phases.  For the 1st time the authors rationalize the amorphization of NaxSb phases by the long ranged strain propagation due to Na-vacancy compared to Li-Sb.  At full discharge, the XRD results show that a minor fraction of hexagonal Li3Sb forms concomitantly with cubic Li3Sb.  The XRD results confirm that Sb crystallizes into hexagonal Na3Sb at full sodiation.  The kinetics of the reaction is assessed by rate performance tests which highlight that both Li and Na can diffuse rapidly throughout micron thick films at room temp.  However, the (de)insertion of Li provides lower overpotentials and larger storage capacities compared to Na.  The difference in rate performance is complemented by diffusion coeff. detns. near the 0 V region where both materials are crystd. into M3Sb (M = Li, Na).  Calcns. show that the energy barrier for near-neighbor vacancy migration, predominant in these close-packed phases, is about twice for Na than for Li.  The anal. tries to relate the lower intrinsic diffusivity of Na compared to Li with the long-range strain propagation induced by the former, thereby leading to an intrinsic origin of differences in rates, mech. properties and amorphization.  Finally, the surface chem. of Sb electrodes cycled in NaClO4 dissolved in pure PC with(out) the addn. of 5% EC or FEC shows presence of ethers and NaF for the EC- and FEC-based electrolytes, resp., and SEI films rich in Na-based carbonates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKpfdtkGeGWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfxJE-KkhuuQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXpslCnurk%253D&amp;md5=50cb05d83d642b77ba72561346e0cd29</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/nl404165c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kravchyk, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Walter, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kovalenko, M.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monodisperse Antimony Nanocrystals for High-Rate Li-ion and Na-ion Battery Anodes: Nano versus Bulk</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Meng; Kravchyk, Kostiantyn; Walter, Marc; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1255-1262</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).  At all C-rates (0.5-20C, e.g. current densities of 0.33-13.2 A/g), capacities of 20 nm Sb particles are systematically better than for both 10 nm and bulk Sb.  At 20C rate, retention of charge storage capacities by 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals can reach 78-85% of the low-rate value, indicating that rate capability of Sb nanostructures can be comparable to the best Li-ion intercalation anodes and is so far unprecedented for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5xNSHYkxGf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOAowjYZLNsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1Wmsbw%253D&amp;md5=6c9a0c090f52077a9b8eda7847cbfe2f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/am504310k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium/Lithium Storage Behavior of Antimony Hollow Nanospheres for Rechargeable Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Antimony nanoparticles anchored in three-dimensional carbon network as promising sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wen; Zhang, Pengfei; Wang, Xuanpeng; Li, Qidong; Dong, Yifan; Hua, Jingchen; Zhou, Liang; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">304</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">340-345</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel composite with antimony (Sb) nanoparticles anchored in three-dimensional carbon network (denoted as SbNPs@3D-C) is successfully synthesized via a NaCl template-assisted self-assembly strategy, followed by freeze-drying and one-step in-situ carbonization.  The three-dimensional interconnected macroporous carbon framework can not only stabilize the architecture and buffer the vol. expansion for Sb nanoparticles, but also provide high elec. cond. for the whole electrode.  Consequently, as a sodium-ion battery anode, the SbNPs@3D-C delivers a high reversible capacity (456 mAh/g at 100 mA/g), stable cycling performance (94.3% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 100 mA/g) as well as superior rate capability (270 mAh/g at 2000 mA/g).  When compared with com. Sb particles, the SbNPs@3D-C exhibits dramatically enhanced electrochem. performance.  Free from expensive template sources and complex manipulation, this work might shed some light on the synthesis of low-cost and high-performance materials for the next "beyond lithium" battery generation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYqJH9BlxHCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOAowjYZLNsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWktLzO&amp;md5=3fc4643288a77027dd91444fa9926cb6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01501H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, X.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lou, X.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb@C coaxial nanotubes as a superior long-life and high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2314-2318</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.  Most importantly, high capacities of 350 mAh g-1 and 310 mAh g-1 can be achieved at large current densities of 10 and 20 A g-1, resp., which represents the best rate performance among the reported Sb-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmon6HTiU9LrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOAowjYZLNsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsVOqsrs%253D&amp;md5=19ea4b459ee66a164418399db8b12d47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/c4cc01326c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lorger, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of One-Dimensional Peapod-Like Sb@ C Submicron-Structures</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">rGO/nano Sb composite: a high performance anode material for Na+ ion batteries and evidence for the formation of nanoribbons from the nano rGO sheet during galvanostatic cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nithya, C.; Gopukumar, S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries exhibit high energy and power densities, thereby making them a promising power sources for multifarious applications.  However, the abundance of lithium (Li) is one of the major crit. issues for using Li battery technologies.  Therefore, for large-scale applications a sodium (Na) ion battery is one of the apt alternatives for portable electronics instead of expensive Li ion batteries.  One of the challenging issues in Na+ ion batteries is the difficulty to understand the chem. involved in view of the large size of the Na+ ion as compared to the Li+ ion, which makes the alloying/dealloying difficult during cycling.  Hence, in this present work, we explore an innovative concept of storing Na+ ions in reduced graphene oxide/antimony (Sb) metal composites.  Such a concept of storing Na+ in the rGO/Sb composite is one of the simplest ways to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal-based anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Furthermore, it is seen that the nano rGO sheet transforms to nanoribbons upon galvanostatic cycling, as evidenced by TEM.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryp-lzHn0P9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOAowjYZLNsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVWrtbbF&amp;md5=0cb4120ef4c51ee603ae519957bf98c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/c2cc32730a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Na-Storage and Superior Cyclability of Nanocomposite Sb/C Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun Sb/C Fibers for a Stable and Fast Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Han, Xiaogang; Xu, Yunhua; Liu, Yihang; Zheng, Shiyou; Xu, Kang; Hu, Liangbing; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzXdqjrNEGhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWht7nJ&amp;md5=382586ead9328ea5a3721bf05276e705</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201304962"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Engelhard, M.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anodes for sodium ion batteries based on tin-germanium-antimony alloys</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Farbod, Behdokht; Cui, Kai; Kalisvaart, W. Peter; Kupsta, Martin; Zahiri, Beniamin; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Lotfabad, Elmira Memarzadeh; Li, Zhi; Luber, Erik J.; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4415-4429</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we provide the first report on several compns. of ternary Sn-Ge-Sb thin film alloys for application as sodium ion battery (aka NIB, NaB or SIB) anodes, employing Sn50Ge50, Sb50Ge50, and pure Sn, Ge, Sb as baselines.  Sn33Ge33Sb33, Sn50Ge25Sb25, Sn60Ge20Sb20, and Sn50Ge50 all demonstrate promising electrochem. behavior, with Sn50Ge25Sb25 being the best overall.  This alloy has an initial reversible specific capacity of 833 mAhg-1 (at 85 mAg-1) and 662 mAhg-1 after 50 charge-discharge cycles.  Sn50Ge25Sb25 also shows excellent rate capability, displaying a stable capacity of 381 mAhg-1 at a c.d. of 8500 mAg-1 (∼10C).  A survey of published literature indicates that 833 mAhg-1 is among the highest reversible capacities reported for a Sn-based NIB anode, while 381 mAhg-1 represents the optimum fast charge value.  HRTEM shows that Sn50Ge25Sb25 is a composite of 10-15 nm Sn and Sn-alloyed Ge nanocrystallites that are densely dispersed within an amorphous matrix.  Comparing the microstructures of alloys where the capacity significantly exceeds the rule of mixts. prediction to those where it does not leads us to hypothesize that this new phenomenon originates from the Ge(Sn) that is able to sodiate beyond the 1:1 Na:Ge ratio reported for the pure element.  Combined TOF-SIMS, EELS TEM, and FIB anal. demonstrates substantial Na segregation within the film near the current collector interface that is present as early as the second discharge, followed by cycling-induced delamination from the current collector.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVb3oOuj1ecbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh2fefyPY0bmQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXkvVyqs78%253D&amp;md5=3b95d3d0fa5e586a5a5c9ce5fb4ec0ce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201504461"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gan, L.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2eYH091soFZoBLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C5CC03825A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manthiram, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Embedded in Graphite: A High-Rate, Long-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous Sb2S3 embedded in graphite: a high-rate, long-life anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Yubao; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous Sb2S3 embedded in a conductive graphite matrix is designed for sodium-ion batteries.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-Dimensional Rod-Like Sb2S3-Based Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Hongshuai; Jing, Mingjun; Huang, Zhaodong; Yang, Yingchang; Zhang, Yan; Chen, Jun; Wu, Zhibin; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19362-19369</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the high theor. capacity of 946 mAh g-1, Sb2S3 can be employed as promising electrode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, the Na storage behaviors of 1-dimensional (1D) Sb2S3-based materials (Sb2S3 and Sb2S3@C rods) are successfully studied for the 1st time, displaying good cyclability and rate capability owing to their unique morphol. and structure.  Specifically, the Sb2S3@C rods electrode presents greatly enhanced electrochem. properties, resulting from the introduction of thin C layers which can effectively alleviate the strain caused by the large vol. change and simultaneously improve the cond. of electrode during cycling.  At a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, it delivers a high capacity of 699.1 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles, which corresponds to 95.7% of the initial reversible capacity.  Even at a high c.d. of 3200 mA g-1, the capacity can still reach 429 mAh g-1.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Insertion in Hollow Carbon Nanowires for Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yuliang; Xiao, Lifen; Sushko, Maria L.; Wang, Wei; Schwenzer, Birgit; Xiao, Jie; Nie, Zimin; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhengguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin and lightweight 3D free-standing Ni@NiO nanowire membrane electrode for a supercapacitor with excellent capacitance retention at high rates</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Nishuang; Li, Jian; Ma, Wenzhen; Liu, Weijie; Shi, Yuling; Tao, Jiayou; Zhang, Xianghui; Su, Jun; Li, Luying; Gao, Yihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A free-standing binder-free 3-dimensional Ni@NiO nanowire membrane is fabricated by a simple filtration method followed by thermal annealing.  With an appropriate annealing temp., the functional nanowires can keep their rough and echinate surface, and the conductive network composed of welded nickel nanowire cores is well-preserved without isolation (0.53 Ω/sq).  The unique 3-dimensional multigrade mesoporous structure not only accelerates the intercalation and deintercalation velocity of electrolyte ions but also provides numerous electroactive sites for the Faraday reaction.  As a result, the supercapacitor electrode can preserve a capacitance retention of 96.1% (36.9 F/cm3) with a high discharge c.d., indicating its wonderful rate capability.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible free-standing carbon nanotube films for model lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chew, Sau Yen; Ng, See How; Wang, Jiazhao; Novak, Petr; Krumeich, Frank; Chou, Shu Lei; Chen, Jun; Liu, Hua Kun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A comparative study of conductive, free-standing, binder-free flexible films made from three different types of com. carbon nanotubes (CNTs), i.e., single-wall, double-wall, and multi-wall was carried out.  The conductive CNT films were prepd. by adding the CNTs to the starting dispersion of carbon black and Triton X-100, followed by a vacuum filtration technique.  These films have been characterized as model free-standing, binder-free electrodes for flexible lithium-ion batteries.  Our expts. revealed that films based on multi-wall CNTs (MWCNTs) are much better than single-wall and double-wall CNTs films in terms of their electrochem. performance.  The flexible MWCNT electrodes show stable cycling behavior and allow up to a 10 C-rate.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKHU3X_DXmMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgEXBOeNis_ZQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXhtVeht73P&amp;md5=74b87b49a069016b4b96cf87a5a7a480</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/nn100619m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, L. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Light-Weight Free-Standing Carbon Nanotube-Silicon Films for Anodes of Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">7</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3671</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3678</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Light-Weight Free-Standing Carbon Nanotube-Silicon Films for Anodes of Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Li-Feng; Hu, Liangbing; Choi, Jang Wook; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3671-3678</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si is an attractive alloy-type anode material because of its high capacity (4200 mA-h/g).  However, Li insertion into and extn. from Si are accompanied by a huge vol. change, up to 300%, which induces a strain on Si and causes pulverization and rapid capacity fading due to the loss of the elec. contact between Si and the current collector.  Si nanostructures such as nanowires, which are chem. and elec. bonded to the current collector, can overcome the pulverization problem, however, the heavy metal current collectors in these systems are larger in wt. than Si active material.  Herein the authors report a novel anode structure free of heavy metal current collectors by integrating a flexible, conductive C nanotube (CNT) network into a Si anode.  The composite film is free-standing and has a structure similar to steel-reinforced concrete, where the infiltrated CNT network functions as both mech. support and elec. conductor and Si as a high capacity anode material for Li-ion battery.  Such free-standing film has a low sheet resistance of ∼30 Ω/sq.  It shows a high sp. charge storage capacity (∼2000 mA-h/g) and a good cycling life, superior to pure sputtered-on Si films with similar thicknesses.  SEM show that Si is still connected by the CNT network even when small cracks appear in the film after cycling.  The film can also ripple up to release the strain of a large vol. change during Li intercalation.  The conductive composite film can function as both anode active material and current collector.  It offers ∼10 times improvement in sp. capacity compared with widely used graphite/Cu anode sheets.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7zPasN1NpeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liquEo5Dr7HUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXmvF2qurg%253D&amp;md5=57d4bf37ba1294a4fd84a545fa3df23a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/jp076883z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cai, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dong, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Fractal Splitting Growth of Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Hierarchical Nanostructures</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pulsed laser deposited Sb2Se3 anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xue, Ming-Zhe; Fu, Zheng-Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb2Se3 thin film has been successfully fabricated by reactive pulsed laser deposition and was investigated for its electrochem. with lithium for the first time.  The reversible discharge capacities of Sb2Se3/Li cells cycled between 0.3 and 2.5 V were found in the range of 530.5-660.7 mAh g-1 during the first 100 cycles.  By using ex-situ x-ray diffraction, transmission electron microscopy, and selected-area electron diffraction measurements, both classical alloying process and the selenylation/redn. of nanosized metallic antimony were proposed in the lithium electrochem. reaction of Sb2Se3.  Sb2Se3 has high reversible capacity and good cycle performance, which makes it potential anode material for future lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqDVqKClaAcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liquEo5Dr7HUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXlvVOgtbw%253D&amp;md5=f5a7751d343f2bc7b67be645484c24c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201002097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhai, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ye, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liao, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Koide, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bando, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Golberg, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Single-Crystalline Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Nanowires for High-Performance Field Emitters and Photodetectors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.
