            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We fabricate high-quality single-crystal Sb2Se3 nanowires using a facile hydrothermal process through careful adjustment of the exptl. parameters, and their field emission and photoconductive properties were examd.  They show low turn-on (2.6 V.μm-1) and threshold voltages (4.9 V.μm-1) and a high enhancement factor (3466).  The individual Sb2Se3 nanowire photodetectors exhibited a marked response to visible light (Rλ and EQE are as high as ∼8.0 A/W and ∼1650%, with a response time of &lt;0.3 s).  Nanowire morphol. was examd. by field emission SEM; the nanowires have smooth surfaces and possess a uniform diam. of 150-200 nm, and a typical length of several tens of microns.  X-ray diffraction shows that all the diffraction peaks can be indexed to an orthorhombic Sb2Se3 phase.  Field emission (FE) measurements show that the Sb2Se3 nanowires are indeed decent field emitters with values comparable or even surpassing those of previously reported ZnO, ZnS, CdS and Si nanowires/nanobelts and carbon nanotubes, suggesting that the present Sb2Se3 nanowires with low turn-on field can be used as practical field emitters.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4AJxI5l-MXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liquEo5Dr7HUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtlalu73E&amp;md5=ee93aa6cad89b43bf60b5ff3acbd2e8d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b11507"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zuo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Organometallically Anisotropic Growth of Ultralong Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Nanowires with Highly Enhanced Photothermal Response</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2819</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2825</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.5b11507</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2819-2825%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DG.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BZuo%26author%3DQ.%2BYang%26title%3DOrganometallically%2BAnisotropic%2BGrowth%2Bof%2BUltralong%2BSb2Se3%2BNanowires%2Bwith%2BHighly%2BEnhanced%2BPhotothermal%2BResponse%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.5b11507&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11544&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.5b11507&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Organometallically Anisotropic Growth of Ultralong Sb2Se3 Nanowires with Highly Enhanced Photothermal Response</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Guihuan; Zhou, Jun; Zuo, Jian; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2819-2825</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultralong orthorhombic Sb2Se3 nanowires have been successfully fabricated via an alternative facile organometallic synthetic route from the reaction of triphenylantimony(III) with dibenzyldiselenide in oleylamine at 180-240 °C without any other additives.  The formation and growth mechanism of the Sb2Se3 nanowires is intensively investigated, and it is found that the anisotropic growth of the nanowires with almost const. diams. is resulted from the synergistic effects of the intrinsic property of the orthorhombic crystal structure and the weak binding assistance of oleylamine, and the length of the nanowires can be elongated easily by increasing reaction time in the synthetic route.  Moreover, the photothermal response of the Sb2Se3 nanowires is first evaluated under illumination of UV light (320-390 nm), and it is esp. noted that the Sb2Se3 nanowires exhibit highly enhanced photothermal responses (more than two times the intensity) as compared to the bulk Sb2Se3.  In addn., the Sb2Se3 nanowires show excellent light-to-heat performance, which is superior to that of the nanostructured titanium dioxide and silicon powder under the same conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6ny1hWUgjubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liquEo5Dr7HUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XltlCktg%253D%253D&amp;md5=ddad7f9ad81f23fa2ce4c8be7aaaa69e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/nn403108w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Langrock, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selenium@ Mesoporous Carbon Composite with Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage Capacity</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">9</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8003</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8010</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn403108w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D8003-8010%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26issue%3D9%26author%3DC.%2BLuo%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BZheng%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DA.%2BLangrock%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26title%3DSelenium%2540%2BMesoporous%2BCarbon%2BComposite%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BCapacity%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnn403108w&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11544&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnn403108w&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Selenium@Mesoporous Carbon Composite with Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Chao; Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Liu, Yihang; Zheng, Shiyou; Liu, Ying; Langrock, Alex; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8003-8010</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Se-impregnated C composites were synthesized by infusing Se into mesoporous C at a temp. of 600° under vacuum.  Ring-structured Se8 was produced and confined in the mesoporous C, which acts as an electronic conductive matrix.  During the electrochem. process in low-cost LiPF6/EC/DEC electrolyte, low-order polyselenide intermediates formed and were stabilized by mesoporous C, which avoided the shuttle reaction of polyselenides.  Exceptional electrochem. performance of Se/mesoporous C composites was demonstrated in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  In Li-ion batteries, Se8/mesoporous C composite cathodes delivered a reversible capacity of 480 mA h g-1 for 1000 charge/discharge cycles without any capacity loss, while in Na-ion batteries, it provided initial capacity of 485 mA h g-1 and retained 340 mA h g-1 after 380 cycles.  The Se8/mesoporous C composites also showed excellent rate capability.  As the c.d. increased from 0.1 to 5 C, the capacity retained ∼46% in Li-ion batteries and 34% in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIbiuPF5puS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liquEo5Dr7HUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1Kltb7N&amp;md5=778fc3935d3408beb58a278cddd0a9ab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/anie.200901723"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dhanabalan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Van Aken, P. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maier, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Encapsulation of Sn@ Carbon Nanoparticles in Bamboo-like Hollow Carbon Nanofibers as an Anode Material in Lithium-Based Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Access to clean, affordable and reliable energy has been a cornerstone of the world's increasing prosperity and economic growth since the beginning of the industrial revolution.  Our use of energy in the twenty-first century must also be sustainable.  Solar and water-based energy generation, and engineering of microbes to produce biofuels are a few examples of the alternatives.  This Perspective puts these opportunities into a larger context by relating them to a no. of aspects in the transportation and electricity generation sectors.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium batteries are characterized by high specific energy, high efficiency and long life.  These unique properties have made lithium batteries the power sources of choice for the consumer electronics market with a prodn. of the order of billions of units per yr.  These batteries are also expected to find a prominent role as ideal electrochem. storage systems in renewable energy plants, as well as power systems for sustainable vehicles, such as hybrid and elec. vehicles.  However, scaling up the lithium battery technol. for these applications is still problematic since issues such as safety, costs, wide operational temp. and materials availability, are still to be resolved.  This review focuses first on the present status of lithium battery technol., then on its near future development and finally it examines important new directions aimed at achieving quantum jumps in energy and power content.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpF3KOlj2NuArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMtSNi806KaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXivF2htQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=7273fa7f9f8dd9462c29aac1df0c7420</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/anie.200702505"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bruce, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMtSNi806KaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHrqX-Ttz-8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01782a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ong, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3680-3688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosFyTQ7K1B3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHrqX-Ttz-8Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1CqsLzK&amp;md5=5a6e72a3ae5ebf92d84322240b2c29cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1149/1.1379565"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahn, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Mechanisms of Lithium and Sodium Insertion in Carbon Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Si-based Li-ion battery anodes are attracting significant attention because of Si's exceptionally high Li capacity.  However, Si's large vol. change during cycling generally leads to anode pulverization unless the Si is dispersed throughout a matrix in nanoparticulate form.  Because pulverization results in a loss of elec. connectivity, the reversible capacity of most Si anodes decays within a few cycles.  Here the authors report a 3-dimensional (3D) bicontinuous Si anode formed by depositing a layer of Si on the surface of a colloidal crystal templated porous Ni metal scaffold, which maintains elec. connectivity during cycling due to the scaffold.  The porous metal framework serves to both impart elec. cond. to the anode and accommodate the large vol. change of Si upon lithiation and de-lithiation.  The initial capacity of the bicontinuous Si anode is 3568 (Si basis) and 1450 mA-h/g (including the metal framework) at 0.05 C.  After 100 cycles at 0.3 C, 85% of the capacity remains.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li23V4QQTofQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta11568b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Baggetto, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ganesh, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, C.-N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meisner, R.                         rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intrinsic thermodynamic and kinetic properties of Sb electrodes for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries: experiment and theory</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Baggetto, Loic; Ganesh, P.; Sun, Che-Nan; Meisner, Roberta A.; Zawodzinski, Thomas A.; Veith, Gabriel M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A detailed comparative study between the electrochem. lithiation and sodiation of pure Sb, relating changes in structural, thermodn., kinetic and electrochem. properties was carried out.  For this purpose, a wide range of measurements using electrochem. (galvanostatic cycling, GITT, PITT), XRD and XPS methods as well as d. functional theory (DFT) based studies have been undertaken.  Assessment of the thermodn. reveals that the reaction proceeds identically during the 1st and 2nd cycles for Li whereas it differs between the 1st and subsequent cycles for Na as the reaction with Na proceeds through a different pathway assocd. with the formation of amorphous NaxSb phases.  For the 1st time the authors rationalize the amorphization of NaxSb phases by the long ranged strain propagation due to Na-vacancy compared to Li-Sb.  At full discharge, the XRD results show that a minor fraction of hexagonal Li3Sb forms concomitantly with cubic Li3Sb.  The XRD results confirm that Sb crystallizes into hexagonal Na3Sb at full sodiation.  The kinetics of the reaction is assessed by rate performance tests which highlight that both Li and Na can diffuse rapidly throughout micron thick films at room temp.  However, the (de)insertion of Li provides lower overpotentials and larger storage capacities compared to Na.  The difference in rate performance is complemented by diffusion coeff. detns. near the 0 V region where both materials are crystd. into M3Sb (M = Li, Na).  Calcns. show that the energy barrier for near-neighbor vacancy migration, predominant in these close-packed phases, is about twice for Na than for Li.  The anal. tries to relate the lower intrinsic diffusivity of Na compared to Li with the long-range strain propagation induced by the former, thereby leading to an intrinsic origin of differences in rates, mech. properties and amorphization.  Finally, the surface chem. of Sb electrodes cycled in NaClO4 dissolved in pure PC with(out) the addn. of 5% EC or FEC shows presence of ethers and NaF for the EC- and FEC-based electrolytes, resp., and SEI films rich in Na-based carbonates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKpfdtkGeGWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li23V4QQTofQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXpslCnurk%253D&amp;md5=50cb05d83d642b77ba72561346e0cd29</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1021/nl404165c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kravchyk, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Walter, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kovalenko, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel composite with antimony (Sb) nanoparticles anchored in three-dimensional carbon network (denoted as SbNPs@3D-C) is successfully synthesized via a NaCl template-assisted self-assembly strategy, followed by freeze-drying and one-step in-situ carbonization.  The three-dimensional interconnected macroporous carbon framework can not only stabilize the architecture and buffer the vol. expansion for Sb nanoparticles, but also provide high elec. cond. for the whole electrode.  Consequently, as a sodium-ion battery anode, the SbNPs@3D-C delivers a high reversible capacity (456 mAh/g at 100 mA/g), stable cycling performance (94.3% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 100 mA/g) as well as superior rate capability (270 mAh/g at 2000 mA/g).  When compared with com. Sb particles, the SbNPs@3D-C exhibits dramatically enhanced electrochem. performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries exhibit high energy and power densities, thereby making them a promising power sources for multifarious applications.  However, the abundance of lithium (Li) is one of the major crit. issues for using Li battery technologies.  Therefore, for large-scale applications a sodium (Na) ion battery is one of the apt alternatives for portable electronics instead of expensive Li ion batteries.  One of the challenging issues in Na+ ion batteries is the difficulty to understand the chem. involved in view of the large size of the Na+ ion as compared to the Li+ ion, which makes the alloying/dealloying difficult during cycling.  Hence, in this present work, we explore an innovative concept of storing Na+ ions in reduced graphene oxide/antimony (Sb) metal composites.  Such a concept of storing Na+ in the rGO/Sb composite is one of the simplest ways to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal-based anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Furthermore, it is seen that the nano rGO sheet transforms to nanoribbons upon galvanostatic cycling, as evidenced by TEM.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryp-lzHn0P9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li23V4QQTofQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVWrtbbF&amp;md5=0cb4120ef4c51ee603ae519957bf98c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1039/c2cc32730a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Na-Storage and Superior Cyclability of Nanocomposite Sb/C Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).  The superior electrochem. performances of the Sb-C nanofibers are due to the unique nanofiber structure and uniform distribution of Sb nanoparticles in carbon matrix, which provides a conductive and buffering matrix for effective release of mech. stress caused by Na ion insertion/extn. and prevent the aggregation of the Sb nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqODsgQsiGAJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liS2Oxe0zsQkg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFKhtrrN&amp;md5=b043a6265ebe5b5183098fbd4c98cc1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC05989A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb Nanoparticles Decorated N-Rich Carbon Nanosheets as Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries with Superior Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liS2Oxe0zsQkg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWht7nJ&amp;md5=382586ead9328ea5a3721bf05276e705</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201304962"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Engelhard, M.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we provide the first report on several compns. of ternary Sn-Ge-Sb thin film alloys for application as sodium ion battery (aka NIB, NaB or SIB) anodes, employing Sn50Ge50, Sb50Ge50, and pure Sn, Ge, Sb as baselines.  Sn33Ge33Sb33, Sn50Ge25Sb25, Sn60Ge20Sb20, and Sn50Ge50 all demonstrate promising electrochem. behavior, with Sn50Ge25Sb25 being the best overall.  This alloy has an initial reversible specific capacity of 833 mAhg-1 (at 85 mAg-1) and 662 mAhg-1 after 50 charge-discharge cycles.  Sn50Ge25Sb25 also shows excellent rate capability, displaying a stable capacity of 381 mAhg-1 at a c.d. of 8500 mAg-1 (∼10C).  A survey of published literature indicates that 833 mAhg-1 is among the highest reversible capacities reported for a Sn-based NIB anode, while 381 mAhg-1 represents the optimum fast charge value.  HRTEM shows that Sn50Ge25Sb25 is a composite of 10-15 nm Sn and Sn-alloyed Ge nanocrystallites that are densely dispersed within an amorphous matrix.  Comparing the microstructures of alloys where the capacity significantly exceeds the rule of mixts. prediction to those where it does not leads us to hypothesize that this new phenomenon originates from the Ge(Sn) that is able to sodiate beyond the 1:1 Na:Ge ratio reported for the pure element.  Combined TOF-SIMS, EELS TEM, and FIB anal. demonstrates substantial Na segregation within the film near the current collector interface that is present as early as the second discharge, followed by cycling-induced delamination from the current collector.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVb3oOuj1ecbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liS2Oxe0zsQkg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXkvVyqs78%253D&amp;md5=3b95d3d0fa5e586a5a5c9ce5fb4ec0ce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201504461"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gan, L.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2eZbQuaj8Xt0N7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C5CC03825A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manthiram, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Embedded in Graphite: A High-Rate, Long-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the high theor. capacity of 946 mAh g-1, Sb2S3 can be employed as promising electrode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, the Na storage behaviors of 1-dimensional (1D) Sb2S3-based materials (Sb2S3 and Sb2S3@C rods) are successfully studied for the 1st time, displaying good cyclability and rate capability owing to their unique morphol. and structure.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C).  Excellent cycling stability is also obsd. at an even higher charge-discharge rate.  A high reversible capacity of 149 mA-h/g also can be obtained at a current rate of 500 mA/g (2C).  The good Na-ion insertion property is attributed to the short diffusion distance in the hollow carbon nanowires and the large interlayer distance (0.37 nm) between the graphitic sheets, which agrees with the interlayered distance predicted by theor. calcns. to enable Na-ion insertion in carbon materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9utH1EdajJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljDZd_mJJ37Mw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XotlShu78%253D&amp;md5=c54fcb809a340c023d9185f1d9f5e848</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C6CP00745G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Additive Free H<sub>2</sub>V<sub>3</sub>O<sub>8</sub> Nanowire Membrane as Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A free-standing binder-free 3-dimensional Ni@NiO nanowire membrane is fabricated by a simple filtration method followed by thermal annealing.  With an appropriate annealing temp., the functional nanowires can keep their rough and echinate surface, and the conductive network composed of welded nickel nanowire cores is well-preserved without isolation (0.53 Ω/sq).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A comparative study of conductive, free-standing, binder-free flexible films made from three different types of com. carbon nanotubes (CNTs), i.e., single-wall, double-wall, and multi-wall was carried out.                         rightTab-cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Light-Weight Free-Standing Carbon Nanotube-Silicon Films for Anodes of Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Li-Feng; Hu, Liangbing; Choi, Jang Wook; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si is an attractive alloy-type anode material because of its high capacity (4200 mA-h/g).  However, Li insertion into and extn. from Si are accompanied by a huge vol. change, up to 300%, which induces a strain on Si and causes pulverization and rapid capacity fading due to the loss of the elec. contact between Si and the current collector.  Si nanostructures such as nanowires, which are chem. and elec. bonded to the current collector, can overcome the pulverization problem, however, the heavy metal current collectors in these systems are larger in wt. than Si active material.  Herein the authors report a novel anode structure free of heavy metal current collectors by integrating a flexible, conductive C nanotube (CNT) network into a Si anode.  The composite film is free-standing and has a structure similar to steel-reinforced concrete, where the infiltrated CNT network functions as both mech. support and elec. conductor and Si as a high capacity anode material for Li-ion battery.  Such free-standing film has a low sheet resistance of ∼30 Ω/sq.  It shows a high sp. charge storage capacity (∼2000 mA-h/g) and a good cycling life, superior to pure sputtered-on Si films with similar thicknesses.  SEM show that Si is still connected by the CNT network even when small cracks appear in the film after cycling.  The film can also ripple up to release the strain of a large vol. change during Li intercalation.  The conductive composite film can function as both anode active material and current collector.  It offers ∼10 times improvement in sp. capacity compared with widely used graphite/Cu anode sheets.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7zPasN1NpeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoh9cd89QVqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXmvF2qurg%253D&amp;md5=57d4bf37ba1294a4fd84a545fa3df23a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1021/jp076883z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cai, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dong, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Fractal Splitting Growth of Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Hierarchical Nanostructures</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb2Se3 thin film has been successfully fabricated by reactive pulsed laser deposition and was investigated for its electrochem. with lithium for the first time.  The reversible discharge capacities of Sb2Se3/Li cells cycled between 0.3 and 2.5 V were found in the range of 530.5-660.7 mAh g-1 during the first 100 cycles.  By using ex-situ x-ray diffraction, transmission electron microscopy, and selected-area electron diffraction measurements, both classical alloying process and the selenylation/redn. of nanosized metallic antimony were proposed in the lithium electrochem. reaction of Sb2Se3.  Sb2Se3 has high reversible capacity and good cycle performance, which makes it potential anode material for future lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqDVqKClaAcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoh9cd89QVqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXlvVOgtbw%253D&amp;md5=f5a7751d343f2bc7b67be645484c24c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201002097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhai, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ye, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liao, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Koide, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bando, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Golberg, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Single-Crystalline Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Nanowires for High-Performance Field Emitters and Photodetectors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">22</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">40</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4530</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4533</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201002097</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-Crystalline Sb2Se3 Nanowires for High-Performance Field Emitters and Photodetectors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhai, Tianyou; Ye, Mingfu; Li, Liang; Fang, Xiaosheng; Liao, Meiyong; Li, Yongfang; Koide, Yasuo; Bando, Yoshio; Golberg, Dmitri</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4530-4533</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We fabricate high-quality single-crystal Sb2Se3 nanowires using a facile hydrothermal process through careful adjustment of the exptl. parameters, and their field emission and photoconductive properties were examd.  They show low turn-on (2.6 V.μm-1) and threshold voltages (4.9 V.μm-1) and a high enhancement factor (3466).  The individual Sb2Se3 nanowire photodetectors exhibited a marked response to visible light (Rλ and EQE are as high as ∼8.0 A/W and ∼1650%, with a response time of &lt;0.3 s).  Nanowire morphol. was examd. by field emission SEM; the nanowires have smooth surfaces and possess a uniform diam. of 150-200 nm, and a typical length of several tens of microns.  X-ray diffraction shows that all the diffraction peaks can be indexed to an orthorhombic Sb2Se3 phase.  Field emission (FE) measurements show that the Sb2Se3 nanowires are indeed decent field emitters with values comparable or even surpassing those of previously reported ZnO, ZnS, CdS and Si nanowires/nanobelts and carbon nanotubes, suggesting that the present Sb2Se3 nanowires with low turn-on field can be used as practical field emitters.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4AJxI5l-MXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoh9cd89QVqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtlalu73E&amp;md5=ee93aa6cad89b43bf60b5ff3acbd2e8d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b11507"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zuo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Organometallically Anisotropic Growth of Ultralong Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Nanowires with Highly Enhanced Photothermal Response</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2819</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2825</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.5b11507</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Organometallically Anisotropic Growth of Ultralong Sb2Se3 Nanowires with Highly Enhanced Photothermal Response</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Guihuan; Zhou, Jun; Zuo, Jian; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2819-2825</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultralong orthorhombic Sb2Se3 nanowires have been successfully fabricated via an alternative facile organometallic synthetic route from the reaction of triphenylantimony(III) with dibenzyldiselenide in oleylamine at 180-240 °C without any other additives.  The formation and growth mechanism of the Sb2Se3 nanowires is intensively investigated, and it is found that the anisotropic growth of the nanowires with almost const. diams. is resulted from the synergistic effects of the intrinsic property of the orthorhombic crystal structure and the weak binding assistance of oleylamine, and the length of the nanowires can be elongated easily by increasing reaction time in the synthetic route.  Moreover, the photothermal response of the Sb2Se3 nanowires is first evaluated under illumination of UV light (320-390 nm), and it is esp. noted that the Sb2Se3 nanowires exhibit highly enhanced photothermal responses (more than two times the intensity) as compared to the bulk Sb2Se3.  In addn., the Sb2Se3 nanowires show excellent light-to-heat performance, which is superior to that of the nanostructured titanium dioxide and silicon powder under the same conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6ny1hWUgjubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoh9cd89QVqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XltlCktg%253D%253D&amp;md5=ddad7f9ad81f23fa2ce4c8be7aaaa69e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1021/nn403108w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Langrock, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selenium@ Mesoporous Carbon Composite with Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage Capacity</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">9</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8003</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8010</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn403108w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Selenium@Mesoporous Carbon Composite with Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Chao; Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Liu, Yihang; Zheng, Shiyou; Liu, Ying; Langrock, Alex; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8003-8010</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Se-impregnated C composites were synthesized by infusing Se into mesoporous C at a temp. of 600° under vacuum.  Ring-structured Se8 was produced and confined in the mesoporous C, which acts as an electronic conductive matrix.  During the electrochem. process in low-cost LiPF6/EC/DEC electrolyte, low-order polyselenide intermediates formed and were stabilized by mesoporous C, which avoided the shuttle reaction of polyselenides.  Exceptional electrochem. performance of Se/mesoporous C composites was demonstrated in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  In Li-ion batteries, Se8/mesoporous C composite cathodes delivered a reversible capacity of 480 mA h g-1 for 1000 charge/discharge cycles without any capacity loss, while in Na-ion batteries, it provided initial capacity of 485 mA h g-1 and retained 340 mA h g-1 after 380 cycles.  The Se8/mesoporous C composites also showed excellent rate capability.  As the c.d. increased from 0.1 to 5 C, the capacity retained ∼46% in Li-ion batteries and 34% in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIbiuPF5puS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoh9cd89QVqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1Kltb7N&amp;md5=778fc3935d3408beb58a278cddd0a9ab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1002/anie.200901723"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dhanabalan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Van Aken, P. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maier, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Encapsulation of Sn@ Carbon Nanoparticles in Bamboo-like Hollow Carbon Nanofibers as an Anode Material in Lithium-Based Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2009</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">48</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">35</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">6485</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">6489</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.200901723</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i6">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.6b11544" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.6b11544</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental section including materials synthesis, material characterizations, and electrochemical measurements. (function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="90f6e7d11eb7775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e7d11eb7775c-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

                    cookie=status;

            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging

    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
